The city's fundraising to purchase aircraft and present them to the government is to commemorate Chairman Chiang's 50th birthday. The naming ceremony of the aircraft is scheduled to be held at 2:00 p.m. on the 24th of this month at the Longhua Flying Port. Respectfully hope that all agencies, organizations, schools, and people from all walks of life will be informed. This is a special announcement.

Japanese Soldiers in Japanese Brewery Once Withdrew Yesterday; More Than Forty More Went There in the Afternoon

The Central News Agency reported that the Japanese troops stationed in the Japanese brewery at the end of Huayuan Street, Zhabei, Shanghai, once withdrew yesterday morning. Then, at 2:00 p.m., more than 40 more Japanese troops went to garrison. The withdrawal situation yesterday morning began at 8:20 a.m. A total of 100 Japanese soldiers and military supplies were loaded into seven military vehicles and withdrawn along Jiangwan Road and Tongji Road to the Japanese military headquarters on North Sichuan Road. It was completed at about 9:30 a.m. When the reporter went to inspect, the army had all withdrawn. There was no trace of the Japanese army inside or outside the factory. Only the Japanese owner of the factory was inside arranging everything. The military supplies and all defense works, such as the watchtower, had been dismantled and taken away. Only a few useless sundries were left on the open space next to the factory. After the nearby residents learned of the withdrawal of the Japanese army, they went to watch in groups. The cowherds were already grazing cattle outside the factory. The area around the Japanese brewery, which had been regarded as a forbidden area for the past two weeks, was restored to its former state. Unexpectedly, at about 2:00 p.m., a Japanese military vehicle carrying more than 40 armed Japanese soldiers, without military supplies, drove to garrison and set up posts around. They did not withdraw until late at night. The situation in the North Sichuan Road area was also slightly eased yesterday, but patrol teams still came and went endlessly and still crossed into the city.

Page 10

Silver Syndicate Handles Rice Mortgage; Method of Rice Merchant's Loan Decided; First Step to Handle Hunan Rice Mortgage to Begin Soon; Silver Syndicate Pays 80% of Price First When Rice is Shipped Out

In order to regulate people's food and help rice merchants, the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications have specially joined Shanghai, Guohuo, Guohua, Yanye, Jincheng, Dalu, Zhongnan, and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to form a silver syndicate to handle domestic rice mortgage. The total amount of loans is tentatively set at 10 million yuan, which is shared equally by the participating banks. The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will act as agents for foreign exchange mortgage matters. The Silver Syndicate Committee has been established and is located in the headquarters of the Bank of Communications. The first step is to handle the Hunan rice mortgage. All qualified domestic rice transported and sold to various places can apply for loans and mortgage exchange according to the Hunan rice sales to Guangdong method. The method stipulates that after the rice merchant's application is approved, the silver syndicate will first lend 80% of the mortgage price. After the rice is transported from the place of origin to a certain place for sale, the rice merchant will return the loan and pay a monthly interest of 7%. If the mortgage transportation period is one year, the annual interest of 8.4% will be paid. The Hunan rice sales to Guangdong has been discussed and decided by the Hunan and Guangdong provincial governments, and cooperation with the banking industry will be carried out. The Import and Export Inspection Committee of the Ministry of Industry will assist the construction departments of the two provinces in handling import and export inspection. The silver syndicate accepts mortgage applications and will review them based on the inspection results. After the Silver Syndicate Committee holds its second meeting within a few days to decide on various procedures, the loan will be started on a specified date.

Kusumoto Went to Beijing Yesterday Morning; Negotiations Before Departure; Japanese Embassy Keeps Secrets

Kusumoto, the chief of the Japanese Army Special Service Agency, who was entrusted with a special and important mission to meet with Commander Tashiro in Tianjin, returned to Shanghai by China National Aviation Corporation plane on the morning of the 17th after finishing his business in Beijing. He also held an informal meeting to exchange views on the steps to be taken in the future. It is now heard that Kusumoto still needs to report to Kawagoe, so he took a car to Beijing at 8 a.m. yesterday (one said he flew to Beijing by China National Aviation Corporation plane) to meet with Suma, the Japanese consul in Beijing, and Utsunomiya, the army attache, to exchange views again, and provide them to Kawagoe for mediating Sino-Japanese diplomacy. Yesterday morning, the reporter of the Ta Kung Pao inquired about this matter to Hachiya Minoru, the spokesperson of the Japanese Embassy, who was tight-lipped about the news of Kusumoto's return to Shanghai. Four Japanese Warships Sailed to Beijing

Thirty-three Foreign Ships Still in the Huangpu River According to the customs report, the No. 22 Japanese torpedo boat squadron of four ships, which were berthed at the Osaka Wharf on the Jiangmian and the Mitsui Wharf in Pudong, suddenly sailed out of the Wusongkou between 3:25 p.m. and 4:00 p.m. yesterday and sailed to Nanjing to garrison. As of now, in addition to the five Japanese warships, there are 25 American warships and three French warships, a total of 33 ships, remaining in the Huangpu River.

Jianghai Ships Report Accidents; Barge Blown Over by Hurricane

Recently, the water level along the Changsha route has receded, only three feet one or two inches. The Shanghai Jianghai ships going to Hunan can only reach Lulin Tan or Jinggang, and then use shallow-water barges to transfer the goods to Hunan. The goods of the Sanbei Company in this port, which were transported from Shanghai to Changsha, were transferred in Jinggang. On the 17th of this month, the company's No. 2 barge, carrying Hunan goods, sailed to the river surface near Ehuashan, when a hurricane suddenly arose and the river waves were turbulent. The barge initially struggled against the wind and waves, but the wind became stronger and the waves became more turbulent. The barge was sunk near Ehuashan. Fortunately, the crew members who fell into the water were rescued because the water was shallow, but the goods in the ship were completely lost, including 50 bundles of white sugar and 50 bundles of pepper. Other goods can still be salvaged. Yesterday, a telegram from Changsha reported that the company had notified the customers in Shanghai who loaded the goods, and forwarded them to the insurance company. On the one hand, it ordered the Changsha branch to send workers to the port to salvage the barge as soon as possible.

Haiyun Crashes into Wharf

The Haiyun ship of the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company came to Shanghai from Lianyungang and loaded a full ship of coal. After unloading at the Zhoujiazui Wharf in Pudong, the ship had to turn around as usual. Unexpectedly, when it turned around in front of the wharf yesterday, its stern suddenly crashed into the No. 2 Wharf of the Zhoujiazui Stack, causing the "small cargo wharf" (this wharf is specially used for unloading small batches of goods, hence the name) to be damaged considerably. The buildings on the wharf were damaged, and the engine blade at the stern of the Haiyun ship was also damaged. After the accident, both parties reported to the bureau. Yesterday, the bureau had sent engineers to the wharf and the ship to inspect the damage situation of both parties.

Changtai Dagukou Run Aground

The Changtai ship of the Minxin Shipping Company is currently sailing along the Beiyang route. The ship was carrying cargo this time and sailed to Dagukou. Due to the low water level in the Haihe River, and the Changtai ship had a draft of 16 feet 6 inches, it ran aground. Yesterday, Shanghai received a telegram from the captain of the ship, saying that the Changtai ship had run aground at Dagukou and had not been able to find a way to escape. Rescue is underway. The Shanghai company could not fully understand the details due to the brief telegram and has sent a telegram to inquire. The Tongcheng ship of the Tongcheng Company ran aground in Chenjiagang, Haizhou on the 18th. According to yesterday's telegram, it had managed to escape at high tide.

Haiyi Damaged Parts

The Haiyi ship of the Huashang Shipping Company in this port has a deadweight of 2,154 tons and a draft of 20 feet 2 inches. The ship is huge and was previously bought and sold with China Merchants and sailed to Nanhua. Now the ship has been rented by the Japanese Datong Company and is sailing to various ports along the coast of North China. Yesterday, the Shanghai company received a telegram from the owner of the Haiyi ship, saying that the parts of the ship suddenly broke down while it was sailing towards Qinhuangdao and it was unable to continue moving forward. It has now found a way to sail to Dalian for repairs. The telegram did not mention how it was damaged, nor did it detail the extent of the damage and the condition of the parts. Those Who Inject Morphine and Use Drugs are Limited to Self-Renovate and Surrender for Rehabilitation by the End of the Year, and are Allowed to be Exempted from Criminal Punishment; Those Who Fail to Do So Will be Sentenced to Death

The Jiangsu Provincial Government issued an order yesterday to the county governments of Shanghai and other counties, stipulating that all those who inject morphine and use drugs must be limited to self-renovate and surrender for rehabilitation by the end of this year, and will be exempted from criminal punishment. The original order stated, "After the general inspection of drug offenders in this province, they should have been eliminated. If there are still those who are obsessed, they should be punished according to the law. However, Jiangsu Province is located in a key transportation hub with convenient transportation. Some may flee from one place to another and hide themselves. Others may be lost for a while and fall into depravity. Article 8 of the Provisional Regulations for the Suppression of Opium and Punishment of Crimes stipulates that those who commit the crimes stipulated in Articles 3 and 7 of this regulation from 1937 onwards shall be sentenced to death. From January 1, 1937, in addition to offenders who manufacture, transport, and sell drugs, who shall still be sentenced to death, other first-time offenders who inject morphine or use drugs, who were originally only sentenced to imprisonment, shall also be sentenced to death. It is not a pity that they knowingly commit crimes, but it is unbearable to see these ignorant people facing the death penalty. In order to show the intention of benevolence outside the law, a final opportunity for self-renovation is given. All first-time offenders who inject morphine and use drugs who self-renovate and surrender to the county government for rehabilitation before the end of this year will be exempted from criminal punishment and handed over to medical treatment for rehabilitation. In addition to separate orders, the county magistrate is ordered to comply, and to widely publicize and inform the local anti-smoking committee and local authorities. The county magistrate must report the situation from time to time."

Xue Guangqian Talks about the Personnel System of Railways in Various Countries; Strict Performance Evaluation, Clear Rewards and Punishments, Layoffs and Salary Increases, and Increased Efficiency

Dr. Xue Guangqian, the current commissioner of the Ministry of Railways, was ordered by Minister Zhang of the Ministry of Railways to visit Austria, Germany, Belgium, Britain, France, Switzerland, and Italy to study the personnel system of railways before returning to China. Yesterday, Mr. Xue came to Shanghai on official business. The reporter specially visited him to inquire about the personnel system of railways in various countries. He gave the following general overview:

The length of railway lines and the number of employees in various countries vary due to differences in population and area. However, the average number of employees hired per kilometer is the lowest in Italy, averaging no more than ten people, and the highest in Britain, about sixteen people or more. This is because after Mussolini came to power in Italy in 1922, he laid off a large number of redundant employees and redundant agencies in the national railways, creating a new look. The British railway industry is not state-owned, but is operated separately by four major private railway companies, which leads to the separation of powers and uneconomical use of personnel. This is due to differences in history, organization, and system, so it is not possible to strongly distinguish between advantages and disadvantages. The most noteworthy aspect of the personnel system of railways in various countries is that not only are the job titles and salary levels of all railway employees unified, but also the number of internal and external employees of each railway is limited to a certain extent, so that the distribution of personnel and the needs of affairs do not lose their balance. In addition to the special selection by the highest authorities of the Ministry of Railways, new employees must go through examination procedures. After passing the examination, they must also undergo

Strict training and be managed by the Ministry of Railways, so that the talents recruited meet the actual requirements. As for the original personnel, performance evaluations are held once or twice a year, which are extremely strict. The reward methods for performance evaluation are generally two types: promotion and grade increase. Grade increase is a fixed salary increase, with a grade increase every year or several years, and a certain salary increase. In addition to passing the examination, promotion must also wait for opportunities. If the railway industry does not develop and there is no possibility of incremental positions, it is difficult to obtain a vacancy for promotion. Therefore, railway personnel are closely related to the railway industry, and everyone takes the development of the railway industry as a prerequisite, because personal promotion is entirely dependent on the rise and fall of the industry. In addition to stopping grade increases or salary reductions, those who do not work hard may be subject to dismissal. Therefore, rewards and punishments are clear, and if rewards and punishments are clear, everything will be done. The railways of Italy have been plagued by many problems in the past, which is known to the world. However, after Mussolini's

Innovation and Reorganization, it has gradually become the norm. Today, it has become one of the countries with the fastest development and the most complete equipment in the railway industry. Before Mussolini came to power, the railways were filled with redundant employees and redundant agencies, and the road administration was corrupt. At the most, the state subsidized the railways with as much as 600 million lire per year. When Mussolini came to power, he carried out major reforms, laying off employees and increasing salaries, so that the fewest people could obtain sufficient living wages. As a result, efficiency increased and results were immediately visible. Within a few years, on the one hand, the state subsidy was reduced to 300 million lire, and on the other hand, the length of the lines was extended, the number of trains increased, and the number of vehicles, locomotives, and stations increased significantly. The laid-off employees were covered by social insurance provided by the state, and the social insurance funds were invested in rural reclamation. That is, this group of laid-off personnel was absorbed into the rural areas. Therefore, when talking about the way to reform politics, unilateral efforts cannot take effect. It is necessary to innovate in many ways and

Collaborate to achieve a common result from the separate efforts of each day. The railway industry is not only a means of transportation, but also a hub of education, culture, industry, and economy in a country. It must be promoted in many ways, and then generate each other to achieve twice the result with half the effort and division of labor and cooperation. The railways of various countries have strict and fair regulations for employee leave rules, travel methods, pension and retirement systems, and various employee welfare programs, which can be used as a reference for the people of our country. I have already prepared a report of more than 10,000 words and presented it to Minister Zhang of the Ministry of Railways, as a reference for our country's reform and revitalization.

Pan Xulun, Li Wenjie, et al. Petition to Amend the Bankruptcy Law; Request the Judicial Yuan and Ministry to Create a Small Bankruptcy System and Clearly Define the Circumstances for Litigation Assistance

The implementation of our country's bankruptcy law has exceeded one year. General bankruptcy cases, due to the limited scope of the estate, are simple and narrow. Yet, they must go through the complex procedures stipulated by the bankruptcy law. In reality, many difficulties often arise, sometimes making the bankruptcy proceedings impossible to continue. Accountants Pan Xulun, Qian Nai Cheng, Li Wenjie, Li Hongshou, and others of this city, noting that various countries have established small bankruptcy systems, such as when the assets of a bankruptcy estate are below a certain amount, procedures like publishing announcements in newspapers are omitted, auditors are not appointed, and court rulings replace resolutions of creditors' meetings. Distributions are limited to one-time payouts. All of these measures are designed to save estate costs and expedite the closing of proceedings. They believe that it is indeed necessary for our country to follow suit. Therefore, they jointly petitioned the Ministry of Justice, requesting an amendment to the bankruptcy law to add a chapter on simplified bankruptcy procedures. The original petition is recorded below:

Submitting a request to forward to the Judicial Yuan and consult with the Legislative Yuan to amend the bankruptcy law and add a chapter on simplified bankruptcy procedures to suit national conditions and facilitate commercial and civil affairs.

We have reviewed the national bankruptcy law, which has been in effect since October 1, 1935, for over a year. Chambers of commerce and courts in various regions have achieved effective results in handling conciliation and bankruptcy cases. We have been selected by the courts in this city to serve as supervisors and assistants in conciliation cases and as bankruptcy administrators in bankruptcy cases. Based on past case-handling experience, we deeply feel that there are many points in our country's bankruptcy law that need to be supplemented or amended. The lack of provisions for simplified bankruptcy procedures is particularly inconvenient. We will first list this point to your department.

We have reviewed that the scale of industry and commerce in our country is generally small, and the private economic situation is mostly poor. The amounts of debts and credits are also generally minor. In recent years, influenced externally by the social recession and internally by unsound organization and improper management, bankruptcy petitions have poured in, overwhelming the courts. Observing the organization of bankruptcy estates, they are mostly incomplete and weak. However, the procedures stipulated by the bankruptcy law must be followed in their entirety. Precisely because of their complexity, creditors' meetings are difficult to convene, auditors cannot be appointed, the management and distribution of the bankruptcy estate cannot proceed, and the bankruptcy administrator is at a loss, ultimately leading to a de facto termination of the bankruptcy proceedings. The development of this phenomenon will cause both the bankrupt and the creditors to suffer losses, greatly deviating from the original intention of the state in formulating bankruptcy laws.

After thoroughly investigating the crux of the problem, it is due to the absence of simplified bankruptcy procedures in the bankruptcy law. Regardless of the amount of property belonging to the bankruptcy estate, all bankruptcy cases are forced to comply with complex procedures. For example, the bankruptcy administrator advances funds to publish announcements in newspapers, but the assets of the bankruptcy estate are insufficient to cover the costs of the estate, resulting in no recovery. Attendees at creditors' meetings repeatedly fall short of the statutory requirements for resolutions, leading to the inability to select auditors. Such examples are too numerous to list.

We believe that to remedy the aforementioned malpractices, the legal intent of setting up simplified procedures in civil and criminal procedure laws should be adopted. A distinction should be made between bankruptcy estates with property valued above a certain amount, which should follow normal bankruptcy procedures, and those below a certain amount, which should be treated as simplified bankruptcy cases with separate simplified procedures. This would aim to save estate costs and expedite the closing of proceedings.

Consider Articles 358 to 366 of the Japanese Bankruptcy Law, which establish small bankruptcy procedures for bankruptcy cases with estate property below 10,000 yuan. The main points are summarized as follows: auditors are not appointed; announcements in newspapers are not required; except for the first creditors' meeting, court rulings replace resolutions of creditors' meetings; distribution is limited to one-time payout. All of these aspects seem to be worth adopting.

Therefore, we specially petition your department to consider the actual situation of bankruptcy cases handled by courts in various regions over the past year and the unavoidable legal difficulties encountered. We request that you promptly forward this petition to the Judicial Yuan and consult with the Legislative Yuan to amend the current bankruptcy law, adding a chapter on simplified bankruptcy procedures to benefit merchants and the public. This would be extremely beneficial.

Furthermore, the bankruptcy administrator's actions during bankruptcy proceedings on behalf of the bankruptcy estate, such as initiating lawsuits, responding to lawsuits, and appealing, are often numerous. In reality, the existing property of the bankruptcy estate is often very limited. The bankruptcy administrator often has difficulty in covering the costs of appeals and litigation at the time. If a request for litigation assistance is made, it is often rejected, and even if approved, it takes a long time. As a result, the administrator is often negligent in pursuing or defending lawsuits, leaving the rights and obligations of the bankruptcy estate unprotected. It should be clearly stipulated in the bankruptcy law the circumstances under which litigation assistance is granted to provide relief.

We also earnestly request that you consider and forward to the Judicial Yuan and consult with the Legislative Yuan to add and implement this provision.

Submitted with utmost anticipation,

Respectfully presented to Minister Wang of the Ministry of Justice.

Salt Inspectorate Plans to Implement New Salt Law, Deciding to Start with Sichuan and Guangdong and Implement Gradually by District System

The Ministry of Finance, in order to reform the national salt administration, has implemented the New Salt Law and has ordered the Salt Inspectorate to be responsible for preparations. The Inspectorate believes that the national salt regions are vast, and the New Salt Law must be implemented gradually by region according to the district system of the salt administration organs. After consulting with the Ministry of Finance, it was decided to begin preparations by district. Considering that the salt administration in Guangdong and Sichuan urgently needs reform and rectification, it was decided to implement the New Salt Law first in the two regions of Guangdong and Sichuan during this period of abolishing the old salt law. The Inspectorate is currently planning and preparing to start on New Year's Day next year, and then the implementation will be decided by salt region.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Issued Order Yesterday to Inspect Meat Cattle; Severe Punishment Will Be Imposed on Those Who Sell and Slaughter Farm Cattle

The Jiangsu Provincial Government issued an order to various business tax bureaus and offices yesterday, stating:

The sale and slaughter of farm cattle that are essential for plowing farmland has always been absolutely prohibited. Only those that are truly old and incapable of plowing are allowed to be used as meat cattle. Orders have been repeatedly issued to strictly implement the Provisional Regulations on Prohibiting the Sale and Slaughter of Farm Cattle and the Implementing Rules. Inspection agencies should strictly inspect those who transport them out of the province and monitor those who slaughter them locally at all times. Meat cattle that have not been inspected and qualified shall not be privately transported into the province or privately slaughtered. If cattle dealers or slaughterhouses privately sell or slaughter farm cattle, they shall be punished in accordance with the regulations and their operations shall be suspended. If the bureau chief fails to comply with the regulations, is negligent in inspection, and allows the private sale and slaughter of farm cattle, resulting in cattle shortages, they will be severely punished upon discovery or accusation to serve as a warning to those who neglect their duties. In addition to ordering the various bureaus and offices, it is hereby urgently ordered that the bureau chief comply and pay special attention.

The Fall of a Literary Giant

— Ke Ling

One

"There must be such a warrior!

"He is no longer ignorant like an African native carrying a shiny Mauser rifle; nor is he tired, like a Chinese Green Standard soldier carrying a box cannon. He does not beg for the armor of cowhide and iron; he has only himself, but he carries the throwing spear used by barbarians. He walks into a field of nothingness, and everything he meets nods to him in the same way. He knows that this nod is the enemy's weapon, a weapon that kills without bloodshed. Many warriors have perished here, just like artillery shells, rendering brave men powerless.

"Those heads each have a battle flag, embroidered with various names: benevolent officials, scholars, literary men, elders, young elegant men, gentlemen... Below the heads are various coats, embroidered with all kinds of beautiful patterns: learning, morality, national essence, public opinion, logic, justice, Eastern civilization.

"But he raised the throwing spear.

"He smiled, threw it sideways, and hit them right in the heart.

"Everything seemed to fall to the ground—but there was only a coat, with nothing inside. The thing of nothingness had already left, having won the victory, because he had now become a criminal who harmed philanthropists and the like.

"But he raised the throwing spear.

"…

"He finally grew old and weak in nothingness and died. He was finally not a warrior, but the thing of nothingness was the victor…

"But he raised the throwing spear—"

—Lu Xun: "Such a Warrior"

Such a stubborn and brave warrior! He hated darkness, detested gentlemen, the vile and cowardly children of "Old China," and the ignorant and brutal rulers... He used an incredibly sarcastic pen to expose and attack them without compromise or timidity. He was regarded as a rebel and reactionary by traditional society, but he was respected and loved by countless young people and righteous people.

Such a warrior—our literary giant Mr. Lu Xun, fought all his life amidst numerous overt and covert attacks, against all feudal and dark forces. Although his spirit had not aged at all, he finally quietly left this world yesterday (October 19, 1936) at five o'clock in the morning.

Two

When I received the news of Mr. Lu Xun's death at around eleven o'clock, I felt a chill run straight from the top of my head to my toes. I was in a daze for a while, feeling extremely empty inside.

The death of such a warrior is an immeasurable loss for China!—In the short history of China's New Culture Movement, what a bright and splendid page Mr. Lu Xun has written!

Around one o'clock in the afternoon, I and several companions hurriedly rushed to Mr. Lu's residence in ×× Village on North Sichuan Road. There was no sound of crying, only a solemn silence and sorrow. Mrs. Lu Xun (Ms. Xu Guangping)'s eyes were somewhat red and swollen, and several young men and women were silently eating lunch. Among these people were Mr. Lu's third younger brother, Zhou Jianren, the editor of "Translation," Huang Yuan, and the young writer Tian Jun, among others.

Led by Mr. Huang Yuan, we went to Mr. Lu's bedroom on the second floor. The room was not large, and Mr. Lu's body lay peacefully on a bed on the left, covered with a pink cotton quilt. A white gauze cloth covered his face. Mr. Huang Yuan lifted the white cloth, and his eyes turned red. Mr. Lu's mouth and eyes were tightly closed. His black hair, with a few strands of silver, his thick eyebrows and beard, and his face, though a little thin, did not look too bad.

Everyone was silent, holding their breath. I felt a heavy oppression in my heart.

Next to the head of the bed, near the window, was a half-old desk, piled with books and manuscripts. Two "Golden Unchanging" writing brushes stood upright in the pen holder. Next to it was a covered porcelain tea cup. This was the place where Mr. Lu had spent so much effort and energy in his life. Now it looked very cluttered. At the end of the desk was the rattan recliner that Mr. Lu had mentioned in his recent article. Leaning against it was a square table, filled with books. There were small bookshelves at the head and foot of the bed. Some woodcuts and oil paintings hung on the walls. One seemed to be a print by Ms. Käthe Kollwitz, and another was an oil painting of a baby, with the words "Sixteen Months After Sea Eagle's Birth" written on it.—Sea Eagle is Mr. Lu Xun's only beloved son, who is only eight or nine years old this year. This innocent child did not seem to understand the worries of life at all and was jumping and bouncing happily.

Looking at these things, I couldn't help but feel deeply moved. This old warrior, our generation's literary giant, has now left us forever!

Three

Mr. Lu Xun was from Shaoxing, Zhejiang Province, originally named Zhou Shuren. He was born in 1881 and died at the age of 56.

In the past two years, Mr. Lu had been very ill. It is said that he suffered from lung disease and inflammation of the diaphragm. A serious illness this summer had worried countless people who cared about Mr. Lu's health for a while, but he eventually gradually recovered. However, his health had not fully recovered.

Many people had advised him to leave Shanghai and go to Japan or another part of China to recuperate, but he refused. When his spirit recovered slightly, he continued his work of reading and writing. "Since last year, whenever I rested after illness, lying on the rattan recliner, I couldn't help but think about what I should do after my strength recovered: what articles to write, what books to translate or print. After thinking and deciding, I would end it with 'That's how it should be—but I have to hurry up and do it.' This thought of 'having to hurry up and do it' was not there before because I unconsciously remembered my age." (Lu Xun: "Death," see "Zhongliu" second issue.)—For the sake of cultural work, Mr. Lu Xun was coping with his limited life in this way!

It is said that Mr. Lu's body and spirit had been very good recently, and Mr. Lu's wife and several close friends were very happy. Not long ago, Mr. Lu also excitedly went to participate in the National Woodcut Exhibition held in Shanghai.

Last Saturday (October 17), Mr. Lu went to North Sichuan Road for a trip and caught a slight cold, but his spirit was still very good. When Mr. Zhou Jianren left Mr. Lu's residence at eleven o'clock in the evening, he was still very cheerful. But at two o'clock, he suddenly fell ill. The symptoms were not very peculiar, only that he was breathing very hard.

He saw a doctor, but it was ineffective, and he finally passed away yesterday morning at five o'clock. He died very peacefully, without leaving any words to his family.—His "will" had been mentioned in his recent work "Death."

Mrs. Lu Xun decided to follow the intentions of that will in handling his funeral.

Four

Around two o'clock in the afternoon, the Star Film Company received the news of Mr. Lu's death and, guided by Mr. Ouyang Yuqian, Cheng Bugao, and Yao Shennong, went to Mr. Lu's residence to take newsreel footage.

The film company shot footage of Mr. Lu's body and his residence, including his desk where he worked, arranged by Mrs. Lu Xun as he used to keep it.

Soon, many of Mr. Lu's friends arrived one after another to pay their respects to his remains. Among these people were many famous writers we know, such as Xia Mianzun, Ba Jin, Zhao Jiabi, Meng Shiyi, and others.

At about three o'clock, the car from the International Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road arrived, and several people carried Mr. Lu's body downstairs wrapped in white cloth. Many people followed behind in silence and sorrow. Mr. Tian Jun, this strong young man, initially lowered his head and wept, and finally cried out loud.

The time for the encoffining is scheduled for tonight. Mr. Lu Xun's body will be on public display at the International Funeral Home from nine o'clock this morning to five o'clock this afternoon, for all those who respect him to pay their respects to his remains.

The funeral committee has been organized, and those participating include Soong Ching Ling, Cai Yuanpei, Mao Dun, Cao Jinghua, Agnes Smedley, and Mr. Lu's two younger brothers, Zhou Zuoren and Zhou Jianren.

The cultural community has not yet decided on what memorial events to hold in honor of Mr. Lu's death. But for such a warrior in the cultural community, a literary giant of China, there should be some expression, even though this may not be what Mr. Lu Xun would have wanted.

Five

I do not want, and in fact cannot, use a worn-out pen to record anything about Mr. Lu Xun's progressive ideas on the Chinese youth, as well as the contribution of his works to the cultural community. His accomplishments will always shine brightly in history, and his outstanding personality will also be a permanent model for all revolutionaries.

Regarding the catalog of Mr. Lu Xun's works and translations, I have written it below based on very limited materials. The time is too rushed, and omissions are inevitable, so I can only correct it later when there is an opportunity. A. Works—Call to Arms, Wandering, Dawn Blossoms Plucked at Dusk, Old Tales Retold, Wild Grass, Hot Wind, The Grave, Huagai Collection, Huagai Collection Sequel, False Freedom, Two Hearts, Three Leisure Collections, That's It Collection, Two Places, Southern Accent and Northern Tone, Quasi-Wind and Moon, Fringed Literature, A Brief History of Chinese Fiction (two volumes), Excerpts of Old News on Fiction, Tang and Song Legendary Collections (ten volumes, compiled and corrected), Selected Works of Lu Xun, Supplementary Collection.

B. Translations—The Workers' Su Hui Luefu, A Young Man's Dream, Ero Shenke Fairy Tale Collection, Peach-Colored Clouds, A Symbol of Anguish, Out of the Ivory Tower, Little John, Thoughts on Landscape Figures, The Wall's Translation, Trends in Modern Art Thought, Lu Gu Hong Er's Picture Selection, The Theory and Practice of Proletarian Literature, On Art (by Lunacharsky), On Art (by Plekhanov), Literature and Criticism, Literary Policy, October, Medicinal Snacks, Destruction, Watch, Dead Souls, Harp, One Day's Work, Gorky's Truth, Bad Children and Other Strange News.

As for a part of Mr. Lu Xun's published but uncollected translations, as well as some unfinished drafts, we will probably know after they are sorted out.

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Has Not Completely Abolished the Purser System on All Ships

Xinhua News Agency reports: Yesterday's newspaper reported that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company decided to abolish the purser position on all Jianghai ships starting next month. A reporter inquired with the company, and the responsible person made a statement, saying that the company added four new ships some years ago, sailing to Hong Kong, Guangdong, and Shantou. At that time, the position of purser was not established. The method, in addition to the cargo handling part being directly under the jurisdiction of the captain, was to set up a general affairs officer to manage the affairs on board, according to the captain's orders. Since its implementation, the business income of the Jianglun ships has also been better since the abolition of the comprador system in April of this year, which was changed to the purser system. Recently, in order to thoroughly reorganize the Jianglun ships, the company sent an inspection team to the ships to conduct on-site investigations. The team was composed of staff from the relevant departments and the new transportation instructor. After more than two months, the inspection of the Jianglun ships was completed. The company reported that some of the pursers on the ships were incompetent or had weak abilities, so they were replaced slightly. At the same time, the new sea ship system was imitated, and the position was abolished. As for the pursers on the remaining ships, if they can work hard, abide by the company's orders, and thoroughly reorganize, the company will still maintain the original system of pursers and will not change it lightly. The report that the company's board of directors decided and submitted to the Ministry of Communications to abolish the purser position on all Jianghai ships is not true.

Yesterday's Journalists Association Held a Joint Meeting of Directors and Supervisors; Price Vouchers Will Be Restored Starting Next Month; Research on the Shanghai Municipal Council's Information Office

The Shanghai Journalists Association held its third joint meeting of directors and supervisors yesterday. Chen Dongbai, Zhu Zhiming, Huang Tianpeng, Wu Shuren, Qian Cangshuo, Sun Menghua, Sun Runshun, Jin Huating, Fan Jinwu, Li Zuting, Hu Zhuoren, Zhu Chaoran, Jiang Zongdao, Gu Zhi'an (Jiang acting), Jin Xiongbo, Shen Qiudiao, Zhang Jiping, Qu Shaoyi (Hao acting), Zhao Junhao, Ma Chonggan, Qian Hua, Ding Ding, Chen Dafan, Xue Nongshan were present. Ma Chonggan presided over the meeting, and Jin Huating recorded the minutes. After the chairman reported on the matters, the admission of Tang Qinruo, Cao Youzhi, Kuang Lixing, Zhang Yingzeng, Xi Hanjie, Lu Xinnong, Shi Hairuo, and seven others as members was approved. Regarding the association's economic problems, the proposal to restore price vouchers, following the example of the previous session, was approved and will be implemented in November. Next, the problem of the Shanghai Municipal Council abolishing the Information Office was discussed. First, Qian Cangshuo and Jin Huating reported on the significance of raising this issue. It was resolved on the spot to organize a committee to handle it jointly with the Daily News Association, and Ma Chonggan, Zhao Junhao, Qian Huating, Yan Duhe, and Xue Nongshan were appointed as members to fully research and handle it.

Saint Mary's Road: Detailed Account of a Bloody Case - A Treacherous Plot to Seize Wife and Property; Chi Wenxiang Nearly Suffered an Untimely Death Due to Deception

At 11 PM on the 14th of last month, a murder case occurred in the loft of No. 38 Tongkang Lane, Saint Mary's Road, French Concession. Fortunately, the victim, with great strength, resisted and cried for help, thus avoiding harm. The assailant, in a panic, fled. With the help of residents in the lane and the police, an accomplice, Xu Yongcai from Pudong, was apprehended and taken to the police station for detention. The injured person was sent to the hospital for treatment. The next day, the police escorted Xu to the Second Special Court for interrogation and investigation. Here is a supplementary record of the case:

The Beginning and End of the Incident

The victim, Chi Wenxiang, also known as Heng Wenxiu, is 29 years old and from Pudong. He married into the Chi family, owners of the Fachang Paint Shop on Gordon Road in the Public Concession, hence the change of surname to Chi. His wife, Chi Wenying, is 27 years old and lives with her husband at No. 7 Ren'en Lane, Baker Road, also running a paint business. Because the Chi family owned real estate, their life was comfortable. Wenxiang's wife had an affair. This tragedy was caused by her lover's plot to seize another man's wife and usurp his property. Chi Wenxiang had a cousin, Xia Boling, who lived at No. 12 Le'an Lane, Avenue Joffre, and

ran a business

at No. 144 Route Beattie. He did not have frequent contact with Wenxiang. On the morning of the 5th of last month, Xia suddenly came to the Chi's house and told Chi's wife, Chi Wenying, that the family of Tang Chang'an, the district chief at the Caojia Road intersection in Pudong, needed to paint their house, and he was there to introduce the business. They agreed to go to the Tang's house with Tang's nephew, Xu Jinfu, the day after (the 6th) to discuss the matter in Pudong. The next morning, Xia and Xu accompanied Chi Wenxiang to Pudong. While walking, as it got late, they suddenly encountered a plainclothes member of the security corps who tried

to make a move midway

to kill Chi. Chi sensed that their appearance was not right. That night, they went to Xia's house and stayed overnight. The next morning, Xia said to Chi, "It's late; Tang may have gone to Shanghai. We will notify you for negotiation after we return to Shanghai." So they returned to Shanghai together. At noon on the 14th of last month, Chi Wenxiang received a phone call from Xu Jinfu saying that his uncle, Tang Chang'an, had arrived in Shanghai and rented

a loft

at No. 28 Tongkang Lane, opposite the Great World. Since Tang was out shopping, they would meet Tang later. Chi then arranged to wait at the Shenqu Theater in the Great World at 6 PM that afternoon. At 6 PM, Xia Boling and Xu Jinfu came to the Great World to meet Chi Wenxiang, and then said that Tang was already waiting in Tongkang Lane. So the three of them left the Great World and went to No. 28 Tongkang Lane. Xia Boling said he had other important matters to attend to and left. Chi and Xu Jinfu walked to the loft at No. 38 Tongkang Lane, where they saw

a villager-looking man

Xu Yongcai, also known as (Xu Yinquan, 23 years old, from Pudong). He was Xu Jinfu's cousin. There was only one wooden board and a large camphor chest in the room, nothing else. They waited until 10 PM, but Tang Chang'an still had not arrived. Xu Jinfu then ordered Chi Wenxiang to sleep there while they waited. So Xu Yongcai closed the door and turned off the lights. The three of them lay down on the wooden board. Before long, Chi Wenxiang drowsed off. The two Xus then took kitchen knives and attacked Chi while he was asleep. Chi felt pain in his sleep and got up in the dark to

resist with all his might

The assailants handed the murder weapon to Chi in the dark. Chi opened the window and threw it out, and loudly shouted for help. The assailants Xu Jinfu and Xu Yongcai panicked and ran out of the door. Chi was covered in blood and, injured, went downstairs and told the landlord Tang Dongsheng about the attack. The accomplice Xu Yongcai was seen fleeing by Cai Jincai, a resident of No. 28 Tongkang Lane. He chased him to the Jiuxing Theater on Foch Road, where he caught Xu Yongcai and handed him over to Chinese Constable No. 801, who took him to the scene of the incident in Tongkang Lane. A phone call was made to the French police station, who

summoned an ambulance

to send the injured Chi Wenxiang to Guangci Hospital for treatment. The assailant was brought to the police station and sent to court for interrogation. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the Second Special Court continued the trial in the First Criminal Court. Gu Shouxi, the attorney of the police department, stated that the investigation of the case had been completed. Because the victim's wife had an affair, after adultery, the suspect intended to seize the wife and usurp the property and committed attempted murder. Xu Yongcai is now being prosecuted for attempted murder. Then, the victim Chi Wenxiang complained about his experience. Xu Yongcai was interrogated and confessed that he was invited by Xu Jinfu, who is on the run. "I did not do it," he stated. The court reviewed the statements and, due to the complexity of the case, decided to adjourn the trial to the 27th and ordered the investigating detective Wu Wengang to summon all relevant witnesses for interrogation next time.

Escort Agencies: Morally Corrupt - City Federation Petitions for Crackdown - Social Affairs Bureau Is Planning Measures

Escort agencies are quite developed in Europe and America and are originally good organizations serving the public and guiding people. They have only been established in China in recent years. Initially, their purpose was still pure, but today, they have sprung up like mushrooms after rain. Only a small number are truly for the purpose of guiding tourists. There are many names and the quality is uneven. Those who operate improperly under the guise of escort agencies are everywhere. According to a recent survey, there are more than 100 such organizations in this city. Because their service purpose is impure, their impact on society and people's minds is quite significant. The Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of this city has petitioned the municipal government to severely crack down on them. Since taking office, Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, has paid great attention to this issue and has ordered the bureau's public welfare and social education divisions to properly formulate disposal measures. Those who truly aim to guide tourists should be allowed to exist; otherwise, they should all be prohibited. The disposal measures are currently being drafted and will be announced soon.

Sale of a Young Girl Exposed - A Group of People Taken to the Bureau for Interrogation

The young girl, Zhang Xiuying, is 25 years old. She lost her parents at a young age and has forgotten her place of origin. She was raised by her stepfather until she was eight or nine years old, when she was sold to Xiao as a servant. A year or two later, unable to bear the abuse, she escaped and became destitute. She met Li Mingshan, a Tianjin native who was acting as a police chief in the Public Security Bureau, who took her home to take care of his children. It has been ten years since then. Recently, Li was dismissed by his superiors and, due to financial difficulties, transferred her to the home of Zhu Chuyang, a Hunan native living on Wufu Road in Pudong, as a maid. After only a month, Li suddenly changed his name to Li Fengyi and colluded with Liu Jinfu, a Tianjin native, who changed his name to Zhang Jinfu, posing as Xiuying's brother, to sell Xiuying to Zhu as a concubine. At 9 PM the night before, they agreed on a price of 200 yuan. Just as they were writing a cohabitation agreement and about to complete the transaction, a police officer on duty at the Beihutang Road Police Station discovered it. He said that the sale of people was prohibited by law and immediately brought Li Mingshan, Liu Jinfu, Zhu Chuyang, and Zhang Xiuying, along with the agreement, to the Pudong branch bureau for investigation. First, Zhang Xiuying testified about being sold. Then, Liu Jinfu pushed the blame onto Li Mingshan. Zhu Chuyang confessed that because his wife could not have children, he planned to take Xiuying as a concubine to have descendants. Director Zhang of the branch bureau, seeing that Xiuying's life was drifting and her situation was pitiful, and that she was not fully developed, found that the defendants' actions were inhumane and ordered that the group of people be taken to the main bureau for interrogation.

Secret Report of Selling Poisonous Drugs - Search Yields Nothing - Deer Fetus Brandy and Guanyin Ten-Drop Water - Previously Sold, But Now Long Discontinued - Jiang Zhang Held Temporarily for Investigation

Jiang Quesheng, from Jiangsu, previously founded the Shanghai Family Hygiene Society on Guling Road, producing Deer Fetus Brandy and Guanyin Relief Ten-Drop Water. After Jiang's death, the Shanghai Family Hygiene Society was taken over by his brother, Jiang Qudan, and moved to No. 18, Lane 434, Baker Road, to continue operations. The Municipal Public Security Bureau previously received a secret report stating that the Deer Fetus Brandy and Guanyin Relief Ten-Drop Water sold by the society contained morphine and other poisonous substances. Therefore, on June 8 of this year, they sent a letter to the First Special Court, requesting

assistance in the investigation

and stating that Baohua Pharmacy at No. 556 Guangdong Road also had Deer Fetus Brandy for sale in its catalog and should be investigated as well. The Special Court then consulted the Laoza and Xinza police stations of the Public Works Department and ordered detectives to first investigate the Shanghai Family Hygiene Society at No. 18, Lane 434, Baker Road. It was confirmed that they had sold the drug, but it was found that the owner of the society, Jiang Qudan, had died in 1931. After Jiang Qudan's death, the society stopped operating, all the drugs were shipped to Jiangbei, and the sign had been removed. Because the police found no evidence, they then went to

Baohua Pharmacy

to investigate. Detective No. 47 pretended to be a customer and asked the pharmacy to buy Deer Fetus Brandy. According to the staff, the drug had long been discontinued, and the current product catalog had also been changed. The detectives also had no evidence, so they reported back to the police station. On July 29, they sent a letter to the First Special Court, which was forwarded to the Public Security Bureau. Unexpectedly, Wu Zhenkang, a relative of Jiang Qudan (a member of the Suzhou Anti-Drug Association), recently reported to the Municipal Public Security Bureau that Jiang Xiangwu, the son of Jiang Qudan, was still selling the previous

poisonous

drugs at No. 15 Chengyu Lane, No. 45 Qingdao Road. On September 12, Wu Hui, together with Chen Youde, an investigator from the Fourth Division of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, went to No. 15 Chengyu Lane, Qingdao Road, and bought four bottles of Deer Fetus Brandy and one bottle of Guanyin Relief Ten-Drop Water, totaling eight yuan, from Jiang Zhang, Jiang Qudan's concubine from Hangzhou. They took them back to the Public Security Bureau and sent them to Jiangsu Provincial Hospital and the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau for testing. It was confirmed that they contained the poisonous substance morphine. Therefore, they requested the First Special Court to issue a search warrant. At 12:30 PM the day before yesterday, they, together with

the Xinza Police Station

and drug detective Yang Yunfeng, went to No. 15 Yongyu Lane, Qingdao Road, for a search, but found nothing. They only found more than a hundred empty bottles on the drying platform. They then took Jiang Zhang to the police station and transferred her to the women's detention center. Yesterday morning, she was escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Wang Yaotang, the attorney of the police station, rose and explained the above situation, stating that the empty bottles seized from the defendant's residence the day before were covered with dust, indicating that they had been placed there for a long time and had not been used. The Engineering Bureau stated that the evidence presented by the Municipal Public Security Bureau was insufficient and that the informant Wu Zhenkang was suspected of

framing the suspect

In addition to objecting to the transfer of the case, they requested that Jiang Zhang be temporarily detained for further investigation, and even if there was a crime, it was within the concession and should be handled by the court. Then, Chen Youde, a representative from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and the informant Wu Zhenkang turned themselves in, proving the situation of buying and testing the drugs, and requested a transfer. Jiang Zhang stated that she and Wu Zhenkang were relatives and that after her husband died, the senior wife fled with Wu's mother, accumulating grudges. Finally, her defense attorney applied for bail, stating that her son Jiang Xiangwu had been detained by the Public Security Bureau. After discussion, Judge Yu Jiang Zhang allowed the detention until Friday for further interrogation.

Western Paint Industry Association Accuses Merchants - Defendant Submits Account Books - Dispute Over a Small Shortage in Rent Collection - Both Parties Have Conflicting Testimony

The Western Paint Industry Association of this city elected representative Ma Shangjie and retained a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Second Special Court's criminal court against merchants Le Zhenbao, Bei Runsheng, Zhang Lanping, and Le Gengrong for a property dispute involving the management of the East New Bridge Foreign Goods Business Association. The case has been heard several times, and the circumstances of suspending the accounts for inspection and verification have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday was the eighth hearing of the continuation of the trial. The defendants, along with defense attorneys Li Zuyu, Lin Yingqing, Yuan Hanyun, Wang Manyun, and Yan Yinwu, arrived at the court at around 3 PM. Bei Runsheng went to Nanjing on business and was represented by his attorney. The plaintiff also arrived with attorney Chao Kun. Chen Shuoying, with the assistance of Clerk Wang Baoxun, presided over the trial in the Second Criminal Court. First, the plaintiff's representative, Ma Shangjie, was asked, "Now that the defendants have submitted the account books from 1925 to 1935, where do you say the embezzlement occurred?" He replied, "Attorney Chao reviewed the case files the other day and discovered that there were discrepancies in the signatures on the minutes of the meeting. Furthermore, they discovered that there were discrepancies in the rent collection, with the rent for the Xinkang Coal Shop being collected more but recorded less, with a difference of 20 yuan per month." The plaintiff should record the defendant's criminal facts in the complaint in accordance with Article 112, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law and requested the court to pay attention. Defendant's attorney Li Zuyu stated that the plaintiff claimed that there was a shortage in the rent, which constituted the defendants' criminal act of embezzlement. He asked whether the plaintiff had discovered any other irregularities. Defendant's attorney Yan Yinwu stated that there was no precedent since the establishment of the court for filing a lawsuit without listing the facts first and then listing them as the defendant's criminal facts after reviewing the account books. The court then questioned the defendants Le Zhenbao and Zhang Lanping about the shortage in rent collection, asking if they had any reply. Le and Zhang both stated that they needed to inquire before they could reply, as they did not know the details at the moment. However, the rent also involved subletting by second and third landlords and tenants, so they needed to rely on the rent receipts. The official ordered the plaintiff Ma Shangjie to check the account books to verify the shortage in rent collection. Ma asked the court to check a line on the roll-over account for 1934 regarding the rent collection from the Xinkang Coal Shop and presented a letter from Han Zhikang, the owner of the Xinkang Shop. Le Zhenbao and Zhang Lanping both stated that they needed to ask Feng Zhengming, the rent collector, about the rent. Le Anrong stated that he did not care about rent collection matters. After reviewing the statements, the court decided to adjourn the trial to the 26th and summon witnesses Feng Zhengming and Han Zhikang for further interrogation.

German Ship's Stevedores Demand Foreign-Based Wages

The Duisburg, a ship of the German Hamburg Shipping Company operating on the Sino-German-American route, docked at the Huashun Wharf in Hongkou after arriving in Shanghai to unload cargo. All the stevedores were contracted by the Fu'an Company on Broadway Road. Recently, a majority of the stevedores joined the labor union and requested the company to change the wages, originally calculated in copper coins, to be based on foreign rates, but this was rejected by the company. At 11 AM the day before yesterday, a dispute occurred while more than 100 stevedores were working on the German ship. Union members and workers loyal to the company argued with each other. As a result, an Indian watchman named Bddar Din was injured in the waist and other parts of his body for trying to instigate a conflict and was sent to the hospital for treatment. By 1 PM, the unionized workers all went ashore together. At 9 AM yesterday morning, the workers hired by the company were unloading cargo, and the union workers boarded the ship again, demanding to join and taking the same steps. For a time, all work on the ship came to a complete standstill. After being informed, the Maritime Customs Water Police Station sent detectives Huang Songsheng and Zhou Zenghua, as well as several Chinese and Western police officers, to board the ship to suppress the situation. By noon, the union workers had been persuaded to leave the ship and go ashore, so the company's workers were able to continue working in the afternoon. It is likely that this labor-capital dispute will be sent to the party and government authorities for mediation.
